### Post by myusername on 2009-11-29
Rules:

1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

EDIT:fail. its only the 29th. my bad guys

### Post by Islington on 2009-12-01
Wow, that was a lot of responses.

> **zagz said:**
> Very nice, I love how that theme (?) blurs out inactive actions.

Thanks, the option is present in Bespin>Button>Toolbutton>Disabled Look.

> **SLEEPER_V said:**
> wow.  that looks great.  what did you do?
I did very little actually, I just modified the Avanti config. Added the winter wallpaper from this awesome [pack]("http://macthemes2.net/forum/viewtopic.php?id=16796408"). Plasma theme is air(default).


> **wishyjr said:**
> WOW! i'd love to know how you put that theme together Islington. Would you mind sharing the wealth?
Thanks, basically the only tweaks to Avanti I have made is to change to change the button shape to metal, and add the showoff=true option, as suggested by the author.

> **koleoptero said:**
> 

You always make themes with all the wow factor they can get. Your screenshots make me feel bad I can't use kubuntu at the moment.
Plus you got two "wow" responses in less than an hour, lol.

How come you turned to so bright a theme though?

Ssss.. convertssss....you musssssttt. Why can't to you do kubuntu? As for the bright, two reasons, bright themes better intergrate the gtk apps I use, and living in florida, this will be the closest I get to snow this year.

> **armageddon08 said:**
> 

Add another wow to that.
@Islington---Awesome work, dude!
Thanks, I didn't really do much. Credit should go to author of bespin and Avanti (same dude)

### Post by tjwoosta on 2009-12-01
> And yes bright themes better integrate with everything (unfortunately?).

Not necessarily. Yes by default everything integrates better with light themes, because web pages are usually light, but you could use custom css sylesheets.

With userstyles you can make web pages match your dark themes, thats what I do. Its does take a bit of effort, but I have somewhere around 30 pages bookmarked and every single one of them has a custom userstyle to match my theme. That covers about 95% of my daily browsing.

You can see a video of my desktop with userstyles here 
(quality and framefrate kind of suck because its my first ever youtube vid and i had no idea what i was doing, but I think you get the point)
[http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dlnuu9lRicU](http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dlnuu9lRicU)

As you can see everything is fairly well integrated, my gtk, gtk2, qt3, qt4, and userstyles all match the same dark theme.

---

### Post by BslBryan on 2009-12-01
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Installation was a fail. Intel drivers suck. ](*,)

The newer versions of Fedora (11, 12) allow you to install the system with a basic video driver.  This should fix your problem.  However, you, in theory, wouldn't even have to try that, since Intel graphics cards have been relatively simple to set up in Fedora.  

Try that, if you want.  It's more KDE than Kubuntu and it's at least a linux distro until you get your laptop.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-12-04
I finally have a new set of screenshots.

GTK Theme: Mac4Lin_GTK_Aqua_v1.0
Emerald Theme: Mac4Lin Emerald Aqua, modified to move the traffic lights to the right
Icons: Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0
Wallpaper:
   Desk 1: A screen grab from the "Studio 60 on the Sunset Strip" DVD, episode 11,  *["The Christmas Show"]("http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0905230/")*
   Desk 2: wallpaper-2-1280.jpg from the [Trans-Siberian Orchestra download page]("http://www.trans-siberian.com/multimedia/downloads.php")
   Desk 3: Ubunchu's [CLI-tan wallpaper]("http://chrislnew.deviantart.com/art/CLI-tan-136062057") from DeviantArt (more available at [http://divajutta.com/doctormo/ubunchu/walls.html]("http://divajutta.com/doctormo/ubunchu/walls.html"))
   Desk 4: drwho_wallpaper_tnd_1280x1024.jpg from the [BBC America Doctor Who Extras page]("http://www.bbcamerica.com/content/123/doctor-who-extras.jsp")

Compiz Effects: Snow, Wallpaper (to get multiple wallpapers, I used [Tombutu's tutorial]("http://tombuntu.com/index.php/2008/07/28/stackswitch-and-wallpaper-plugins-with-compiz-076/")), Expo (to make third screenie)

Programs:
[AWN trunk]("http://awn.planetblur.org/?action=g_reply&ID=1490") applets: Cairo Main Menu; launchers for Chromium, Evolution, Pidgin, Epiphany, Terminal (via the Launcher/Taskmanager applet); SlickSwitcher, Awn System Monitor, Awn Terminal Applet, Volume Control, Garbage, Quit-Logoff applet
[Minitube]("http://flavio.tordini.org/minitube") (in [Christian Mangold's PPA]("https://launchpad.net/~neversfelde/+archive/ppa"), slightly newer version available at GetDeb)
Sonata
[Screenlets]("http://www.screenlets.org/"): ClockScreenlet (in default package), [Graphical System Stats]("http://screenlets.org/index.php/Graphical_System_stats")
[Google Gadgets (for Linux]("http://code.google.com/p/google-gadgets-for-linux/")) Sidebar: [WeatherBug Sidebar Gadget]("http://desktop.google.com/plugins/i/weatherbug.html?hl=en"), and three instances of [No-frills Google Mail]("http://desktop.google.com/plugins/i/nfgmail_521.html?hl=en") (both gadgets in the basic install from the universe repo)

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-12-04
> **whiskeylover said:**
> How? I can't see an option to do that in AWN :(

You can't change the position of AWN. You can only move it up or down with Configuration Editor. You could move it to the sides, but the dock will remain horizontal.

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-12-06
> **red33m said:**
> The time is fabulous...!!! How did you do it??

Take the details [from this post]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=8446369&postcount=364")
Extract the .conkyrc and .lua.lua scripts to your home folder. Install conky (sudo apt-get install conky) and run it. Simple as a pie. Although I doubt it would fit well in the KDE desktop. You can experiment as much as you want though, it doesn't affect anything else.

> Oh, whoops lol :) Didn't read everything. Still, feels like every second post is asking for your panel :lolflag:

Here's the repo:

```
#### Avant Window Navigator (AWN Testing Team - Trunk Builds)
## sudo apt-key adv --recv-keys --keyserver keyserver.ubuntu.com BF810CD5
deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/awn-testing/ppa/ubuntu karmic main
```

### Post by Uncle Spellbinder on 2009-12-07
Or use a host like [Image Socket](http://www.imagesocket.com/) or [ImageShack](http://www.imageshack.us/). Much better than using attachments. 

Upload your image to one of the above and you'll get a "fotum code". Paste that code in your post and you're good to go.

---

That's in your signature but I'd really like your help please.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-12-07
> **chickengirl said:**
> Talking of thumbnails -- is there a simple way to do those in photobucket that I'm missing? I've used it for years but now their interface has all this java/javascript crap that my browser doesn't like and it's getting really hard to navigate.


Place a checkmark by the filename of the picture you want a thumbnail for and scroll to the bottom of the page.  Click "Generate HTML and IMG code."

Copy and paste everything in the "IMG clickable thumbnails for message boards" box.

### Post by TheNessus on 2009-12-07
> **Berk said:**
> Nothing special in the least, and now I've looked at this thread again, rather dull and prone to being radically altered.
A question though, I've started using a double wide bar for when I'm doing assignments so I can have more articles and the like visible, but is there a way I can stop the other icons being so damned huge?


Yes, you could make the bottom panel not to expand, and have only the notification area in it. Put this panel at the right Then have another non-expanded panel at the left with your tasks, make it double. 

Like this (made it especially for you, heh):
[[IMG]http://www.picamatic.com/show/2009/12/08/02/43/6291379_bigthumb.png[/IMG]]("http://www.picamatic.com/view/6291379_Screenshot/")

Or you could do what I do, use DockbarX, to remove the text from tasks and save more space:

[[IMG]http://www.picamatic.com/show/2009/12/04/09/31/6191002_bigthumb.png[/IMG]](http://www.picamatic.com/view/6191002_Screenshot/)

### Post by andrek on 2009-12-08
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Could I get your font face, size, DPI and hinting details, please?

I'm using Aller Regular 9 as the application font, Segoe UI Semibold 9 as the emerald font with 96 DPI, subpixel smoothing and hinting set to "none".

Oh and Lucida Sans Regular 10 as the menubar font and Neutra Text TF Light SC Alt Bold 7 for the desktop icons' fonts.

> **pelle.k said:**
> Hey, thats really good! I i thought it was a pimped out OS X install for a while there. Nautilus ultimately gives it away though.
What's the window border and gtk?

Nautilus is the weakest point here, even though I have already applied two patches and recompiled it. Still needs some work, especially with the toolbar.

Window border theme is based on narf41's gruenstich ( available on deviantart ) and the gtk theme is also a modification of gruenstich.

And thanks for your kind opinion :)

### Post by tjwoosta on 2009-12-08
> **koleoptero said:**
> How did you get vlc to look ok in openbox? It looked like hell in mine. I ditched it and installed gnome-mplayer instead. lol

Not my screenshot, but vlc use qt whereas gnome-mplayer uses gtk. I believe he just changed his qt theme to match the gtk and openbox themes. Its really easy to do.

Just use
```
qtconfig
```

For qt3 apps you can use
```
qt3config
```

I use arch and qtconfig is installed by default whenever you install any qt apps, but Im not sure how it works in debian distros. I assume it would be the same, buy you may need to search synaptic for qtconfig and install the package separately.

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-12-08
> **armageddon08 said:**
> What Plasma theme is that and what's the name of that lyrics downloading widget?
The plasma theme is Blackglass. The lyrics widget is a plasmoid that I've been working on for a while now. You can try it out [here]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/lyrics-display.plasmoid"). It requires the packages python-qt4 python-kde4 plasma-scriptengine-python python-beautifulsoup and should work with about any music player that you care to use.

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-12-08
> **koleoptero said:**
> I know about qtconfig and stuff, *but* the mystery is that when I'm using gnome vlc looks cool, but when I logout and login to openbox it looks like cr*p. Not like oxygen or something, genuine cr*p. Same applies for openoffice which is not qt lol.

EDIT: sorry if I sound ungrateful, I'm not, really. :)

I have no problem with qtconfig on Openbox. You have run qtconfig while on Openbox instead of while on Gnome? To make OpenOffice mimic your Gtk+ theme, add this to **.config/openbox/autostart.sh** (or .xinitrc if you use this file):
```
export OOO_FORCE_DESKTOP="gnome"
```

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-12-08
> **danielrmt said:**
> I have no problem with qtconfig on Openbox. You have run qtconfig while on Openbox instead of while on Gnome? To make OpenOffice mimic your Gtk+ theme, add this to **.config/openbox/autostart.sh** (or .xinitrc if you use this file):
```
export OOO_FORCE_DESKTOP="gnome"
```

Thank you, that indeed fixed the openoffice thing (even the quickstarter works now). :) I must keep notes on stuff for the day I'll permanently move to openbox :P

### Post by MooPi on 2009-12-08
Just a simple media box. No panels , conky, or desktop widgets. Just Openbox with autostart of alsamixer, file manager and htop. If you'll notice the 48 mb  of use in htop, this is a stripped down puppy. Atom cpu isn't taxed by the light load and is quick and responsive. Would use less if I didn't have any thing load at startup.

### Post by sertse on 2009-12-09
Did some changes to get Speck's Macchiato to work right with Xfce Panel like it does in Gnome panel.  Followed the documentation here [http://wiki.xfce.org/tips#gtkrc_files](http://wiki.xfce.org/tips#gtkrc_files) The first bit are the original settings, the latter are my changes. Messy and duplicate, but who cares. 

```
#Panel
widget "*PanelWidget*" 					style "murrine-panel"
widget "*PanelApplet*" 					style "murrine-panel"
widget "*fast-user-switch*"				style "murrine-panel" # Workaround for Fast User Switch applet
class "PanelApp*" 					style "murrine-panel"
class "PanelToplevel*" 					style "murrine-panel"
#The panel menubar
widget_class "*Panel*<GtkMenuBar>*"           		style:highest "murrine-panel"

#XFCE Panel

widget_class "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
widget "*PanelWidget*" style "murrine-panel"
widget "*PanelApplet*" style "murrine-panel"
widget "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
widget_class "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
class "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
class "*Tray*" style "murrine-panel"
class "*tray*" style "murrine-panel"
```

Old (from my earlier post in the screnshot thread: 
[[IMG]http://imgur.com/CYOAIs.png[/IMG]](http://imgur.com/CYOAI.jpg) 

Now
[[img]http://omploader.org/tMnlobQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMnlobQ)

I like dark panels.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-12-09
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Hi all...Haven't done much lately as I've been working on the same GTK theme for bloomin' ages now...Call it a learning curve!

Anyway, any of you GTK theme geniuses know how to make menus dark ONLY if they drop down from a menubar?  I want those to be dark and the rest (right-click, panel, etc.) to be light...I'm not even sure it can be done!

TIA :)I imagine it's similar to creating 'sub themes' for any widgets embedded in a notebook.
```
class "GtkMenu"			style "theme-1"
class "GtkMenuItem"		style "theme-1"
widget_class "*MenuItem.*"	style "theme-1"

class "*MenuBar*"		style "theme-2" # menubar
widget_class "*MenuBar.*"	style "theme-2" # menubar item

class "*MenuBar*GtkMenu*"	style "theme-3" # needs to be something like this
class "*MenuBar*GtkMenuItem*"	style "theme-3" # needs to be something like this
```
Be sure to have your matches in that order. If you put the general GtkMenu match after the MenuBar*GtkMenu match, the general one will overwrite the latter one.

> **sertse said:**
> Did some changes to get Speck's Macchiato to work right with Xfce Panel like it does in Gnome panel.  Followed the documentation here [http://wiki.xfce.org/tips#gtkrc_files](http://wiki.xfce.org/tips#gtkrc_files) The first bit are the original settings, the latter are my changes. Messy and duplicate, but who cares. 

```
#Panel
widget "*PanelWidget*" 					style "murrine-panel"
widget "*PanelApplet*" 					style "murrine-panel"
widget "*fast-user-switch*"				style "murrine-panel" # Workaround for Fast User Switch applet
class "PanelApp*" 					style "murrine-panel"
class "PanelToplevel*" 					style "murrine-panel"
#The panel menubar
widget_class "*Panel*<GtkMenuBar>*"           		style:highest "murrine-panel"

#XFCE Panel

widget_class "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
widget "*PanelWidget*" style "murrine-panel"
widget "*PanelApplet*" style "murrine-panel"
widget "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
widget_class "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
class "*Panel*" style "murrine-panel"
class "*Tray*" style "murrine-panel"
class "*tray*" style "murrine-panel"
```

The Xfce window matches are wrong. Besides many simply being redundant duplications of the gnome-panel matches, your first one needs to be more specific than simply, "*Panel*", as it'll screw with applications like gedit and Exaile, whose sidebars are called panels. The match needs to be "*Xfce*Panel*"

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-12-10
What the hell is wrong with the forums today? :mad:

Anyway...

**@rhart211:** I assume you installed the hydroxygen iconset. If you navigate in its folder (.icons/hydroxygen) you'll see a customizing-instructions file which you should read :P But since I'm in an exceptionally good mood today I'll make it easy.

Open a terminal and type:

cd .icons/hydroxygen
chmod +x change-type.sh

then open the image customize!!.jpg in that folder and apply whatever icon change you want from there by typing in the terminal (in that folder again):

change-type.sh string_that_apllies_the_change

for example to get the blue gnome foot icon: change-type.sh gnome-blue

after you finish all the changes load another iconset and then again the hydroxygen iconset and you'll see all the changes applied.

**@chickengirl:**Thank you, I love the simplicity of this wallpaper. :KS

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-12-11
> **MattDobson said:**
> Thank you.  I don't know how to remove the shadow, how do I go about removing it?

Here is the wallpaper:

[http://ipapun.deviantart.com/art/Love-your-Nature-144819914](http://ipapun.deviantart.com/art/Love-your-Nature-144819914)

Install compizconfig settings manager if you don't already have it: sudo apt-get install compizconfig-settings-manager
Then open it in the preferences menu (system -> preferences).
Locate the "window decorations" button and press it. In the page that opens you'll see a "Shadow windows" line where you can type. Enter this: (any) & !(class=Gnome-panel)
You're ready.

And thank you for the wallpaper.

---

### Post by Dobbie03 on 2009-12-11
> **koleoptero said:**
> Install compizconfig settings manager if you don't already have it: sudo apt-get install compizconfig-settings-manager
Then open it in the preferences menu (system -> preferences).
Locate the "window decorations" button and press it. In the page that opens you'll see a "Shadow windows" line where you can type. Enter this: (any) & !(class=Gnome-panel)
You're ready.

And thank you for the wallpaper.

Anytime. Thanks for the help, I just worked it out myself.  :)

### Post by gutterslob on 2009-12-11
> **The Real Dave said:**
> Decided to change Conky. Good or Bad? :)
[[snip]]
  

You could try making everything fit the darker grey bar... looks like you can pull it off if you get the shade just right.
Why is your temperature red?.. did you set it to always show up as red or is it more of a warning? (39.5 deg doesn't seem like a dangerous level... even most Atom processors idle around that temp)

Regarding the red bar in Chromium, I ran into that problem as well at one time, never really bothered to look at the cached theme folder. I just changed to the default blue chromium theme and then back again to the one I was using ( [https://tools.google.com/chrome/intl/en/themes/google.html](https://tools.google.com/chrome/intl/en/themes/google.html) ) and the problem went away.
 
Agricultural method, but it worked.

### Post by ddnev45 on 2009-12-12
> **koleoptero said:**
> Yeah I use feh, though if you could help me with a command to add to the startup to re-set the wallpaper I'd be thankful :lolflag: the icons on the desktop didn't fit minimalism.

From: [Urukrama's guide to configure openbox]("http://urukrama.wordpress.com/openbox-guide/#Feh")

> 7.1.1 Wallpapers with Feh

Feh is a very fast and light image viewer that is also capable of setting the wallpaper. This is a simple method, but my favourite. First we need to install Feh:

	sudo aptitude install feh

Once you have Feh installed, you can set a wallpaper with Feh using one of the following commands:
#

      To scale the image:

		feh --bg-scale “/path/to/image”

#

      To tile the image:

		feh --bg-tile “/path/to/image”

#

      To centre the image:

		feh --bg-center “/path/to/image”

If you use Feh also as an image viewer, open the image, right click on it and go to File > Background and select your preferred option. If you use Thunar, you can also create a custom action (Edit > Configure custom action > ). Create a new action called ‘Set as Background’ and use the following command: feh –bg-scale %f (or tile/center/etc.) and select ‘Image files’ in the ‘Appearance condition’ tab. Now you’ll just have to right click on an image file in Thunar and select the ‘Set as Background’.

To make sure Feh loads the wallpaper again when you start Openbox, add this to your autostart file (see above):

.HOME/.fehbg &

Why is your temperature red?.. did you set it to always show up as red or is it more of a warning? (39.5 deg doesn't seem like a dangerous level... even most Atom processors idle around that temp)

Regarding the red bar in Chromium, I ran into that problem as well at one time, never really bothered to look at the cached theme folder. I just changed to the default blue chromium theme and then back again to the one I was using ( [https://tools.google.com/chrome/intl/en/themes/google.html](https://tools.google.com/chrome/intl/en/themes/google.html) ) and the problem went away.
 
Agricultural method, but it worked.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-12-13
> **snakeman21 said:**
> I, for one, would like to know how you got your menu to be transparent... That's sweet!

Compiz config manager > Opacity, Brightness and Saturation plugin. For the matching, use:```
(type=Menu | PopupMenu | DropdownMenu)
```

P.S. - I believe the xorg.conf file isn't missing because someone forgot to create it. It's just *[COLOR=DimGray]hidden[/COLOR]*. If you need one, you can create it.

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-12-13
> **Physical Hook said:**

P.S. - I believe the xorg.conf file isn't missing because someone forgot to create it. It's just *[COLOR=DimGray]hidden[/COLOR]*. If you need one, you can create it.

I tried what several sites proposed to make xcompmgr work and they didn't. So I just created the file with just the 3 lines it needed, then added a string at the autotart file and it worked. lol.

Xcompmgr shadow values were recommended by tjwoosta, btw... so cheers to him!!

I'm starting to miss my grey, though :(

It's the wallpaper I bet. There's nothing on the desktop and conky is as minimal as it gets (unless I change words with icons lol).

I like my compositing values. The thing I missed are the fadeout/fadein for closing/opening things which is sooooo smooth it makes compiz seem raw and clunky.

If you feel better with grey then go back to it. I like your desktops when I see them, and I liked mine yesterday but after several hours of a fully grey desktop I caught myself being angry at my computer. Truly. lol

BTW if you use firefox, and you switch to a grey desktop again, try the [full flat theme]("https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/6971") combined with the [hide favicons addon]("https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/7031") if you use the bookmarks bar. It really looks good on grey.

EDIT: I also switched to nitrogen for the wallpapers, thanks for pointing it out.

### Post by gutterslob on 2009-12-16
> **The Real Dave said:**
> Mine for today, festive :) Got the wallpaper here, its a few pages back I think :)

[[IMG]http://omploader.org/tMzBkaA[/IMG]]("http://omploader.org/vMzBkaA")

Changed theme to use Murraine engine for clear panels, changed conky, and added transparency to menus and terminals. Opinions would be nice :)

I'm not really familiar with customizing Gnome. (I do have Debian + gnome on my workstation, but it's almost stock in terms of looks)

Looks good, but I've never been a fan of clear gnome panels (the workspace switcher always looks dodgy with them).... you might want some solid, metallic/icy panels... try the Showtime or Infinity themes from the Bisigi project ( PPA = [https://launchpad.net/~bisigi/+archive/ppa]("https://launchpad.net/%7Ebisigi/+archive/ppa") )

Your conky would do well with a dark blue colour as well... use the eyedropper to get the value of the darker blue in the wallpaper and use that for your conky.

That's all I can offer. Don't know if it's helpful or not.

Cheers.

---

### Post by marco123 on 2009-12-16
> **The Real Dave said:**
> How did you get those screenlets? :)

> sudo apt-get install screenlets

Applications>Accessories>Screenlets to bring up the manager and double-click the "RingSensors" screenlet.  You have to configure each one (3 in my case) by selecting which cpu/ram you want each of them to monitor.

Added screenshot.

### Post by Guitar John on 2009-12-17
Xubuntu 9.10
Default theme is called "Albatross."  Unfortunate name, nice theme.

The top panel is set to Full Width, 20 pixels.
The bottom panel is set to Normal Width, 32 pixels.

I moved the Notification Area and  Mixer Plug-in to the bottom panel.  I created launchers for Firefox, Thunderbird, Pidgin, and xfce4-terminal.  Post screenshot, i added Exaile and eTktab.

The wallpaper is called First Spaceflight.

### Post by nibirumarduk on 2009-12-17
> **cdwillis said:**
> @nibirumarduk Why did you post a link to pastebin instead of just pasting your links in your post? :)

cdwillis, for a good few reasons.
Firstly, there is a limitation on the size and resolution of the attachments for ubuntuforums. If you are unaware, do check it out and then compare with the resolution of my screenies with that limitation ;)

Secondly, I have 6 screenies in total there. Imagine how it'll affect a typical forum user here i.e. in terms of page loading speed.

Last but not least, to explore some unorthodox usage of the pastebin service :P

Good enough reasons cdwillis? :popcorn:

### Post by nibirumarduk on 2009-12-17
> **sertse said:**
> [[img]http://omploader.org/tMzBsZA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMzBsZA) [[img]http://omploader.org/tMzBsZQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMzBsZQ)


Albatross (Xubuntu default) is a fine theme, period. I found I deliberate went back to extract it, so I can use it in Arch..

Uncluttered, simple yet beautiful desktop.

On a separate issue, while I appreciate that users with sight problems may find them useful, I simply hate icons on the desktop as well as those in menu entries along with buttons. There were ways to remove them in Jaunty. But too bad with the changes in upstream GNOME, no matter how I tried (see below), the furthest I got to was to have them removed from applications but they still are there in the main menu.

These used to work in Jaunty,
1.
In GConf Editor, desktop -> gnome -> interface -> buttons_have_icons -> DISABLED and also menus_have_icons -> DISABLED

2.
Preferences -> Appearance -> Interface -> unchecking the box that says "Show icons in menus"
But sadly, not anymore. At least not for the icons in the Main Menu :(

Shouldn't users be given the choice not to have them? Or at least an easy way of doing so?

---

### Post by Islington on 2009-12-17
> **rkakkar said:**
> i've just done a fresh install of kubuntu 9.10 and i want my system to look just like this! can you help  out?
Well okay, please keep in mind that kde 4.4 is in beta, and has crashed twice for me without warning (well... x-session crashed) in only 17 hrs of runtime. Also certain, plasma-widgets still don't work (read: will crash plasma). you may wish to stick with 4.3.4 for stability.


now with that disclaimer done: add the kubuntu beta repository to your sources and update your system. [(link)]("http://www.kubuntu.org/news/kde-sc-4.4-beta-1")

Now the changes I made:

Style: Oxygen
Windows: Oxygen> Border Size tiny> Fine tuning >outline active window title.(the tabbing is f*ing amazing...I may have KDE do it automatically)
Color scheme: my own; attached.
Wallpaper: stolen from opensuse by nuno pinheiro. (attached)
Several odd plasmoids, on 4 different activities.
Added weather and device manager inside the systemtray plamoid.
Fonts: Segoe Semibold 9
Tweak the effects for animation speed, use lancelot launcher instead of the default.

> **myusername said:**
> i HAVE to have details
:) thanks. I have written down most of my changes, is there anything else?

My desktop is actually not looking like that now, since I am playing around and purposefully breaking plasma.

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-12-18
> **-Phi- said:**
> Nethack!
it is addictive!

> **Felliph3 said:**
> Conky setup? Very useful!
sure
```
update_interval 1.0
double_buffer yes
background no
 
# Geometry
alignment top_left
gap_x 10
gap_y 2
maximum_width 1420
minimum_size 1420
 
# Create own window
own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
#own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
 
use_xft yes
uppercase no
override_utf8_locale yes
short_units yes
 
# Appearance
xftfont Aller:size=9
color0 808080
color1 ffffff
color2 999999

TEXT
${goto 1}${font Aller:size=9}$color0${pre_exec lsb_release -is} $color1${pre_exec lsb_release -rs}$color0 : Kernel $color1$kernel $color2$machine$color0 : updates $color1${execi 3600 aptitude search '~U' | wc -l | sed 's/^0$/none/'}$color0  ::  RAM $color1$mem$color2/$memmax$color0 : Swap $color1$swap$color2/$swapmax$color0 : CPU $color1$cpu%$color0  ::  Root $color1${fs_used /}$color2/${fs_size /}$color0  Home $color1${fs_used /home}$color2/${fs_size /home}$color0  ::  Download $color1${downspeed wlan0}$color0  :  Upload $color1${upspeed wlan0}$color0$alignr${time %d %b}  $color1${font Aller:bold:size=11}${time %H:%M}   
```

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-12-19
> **Kuro-Chinko said:**
> Very clean look. :)  Nethack is win.

I more prefer all the openbox shots here, but I'm still new to Ubuntu and I'm scared to try.

Openbox is great and very very customizable! You can [install Openbox]("apt:openbox,obconf,obmenu") alongside Gnome or KDE and choose it on login. You have to tweak it a little to have a wallpaper, network connection, etc, as Openbox is only the window manager and the root menu (this looks a bad thing at first, but this is exactly why OB is so customizable). You can also try [Crunchbang Linux]("http://crunchbanglinux.org/"), an Ubuntu derivative which works out-of-the-openbox :), but their last version is based on 9.04 not 9.10.

---

### Post by Schendje on 2009-12-19
Sort of clean:

[[IMG]http://img130.imageshack.us/img130/6205/screenshotgru.th.png[/IMG]](http://img130.imageshack.us/i/screenshotgru.png/)

Dirty:

[[IMG]http://img130.imageshack.us/img130/5606/screenshotdirty.th.png[/IMG]](http://img130.imageshack.us/i/screenshotdirty.png/)

Theme is the regular Ubuntu Karmic one, but with grey instead of brown. Music thingy is a Screenlet with Exaile's Desktop Cover plug-in above it. Yeah, it's a workaround. :D Does anyone know if Exaile can send album art to the screenlet directly?

Conky:

```
# conky configuration

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background yes

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont :size=8

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.8

# Print everything to console?
out_to_console no

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
#own_window no
#own_window_type desktop # Try also 'normal' or 'override'
#own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
#own_window_transparent no

own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager


# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline yes

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment bottom_left

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 40
gap_y 60

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

#${color 9A9A9A}cpu ${color FFFFFF}${cpu cpu1}+${cpu cpu2} | 
#${color 9A9A9A}dwn ${color FFFFFF}${downspeed wlan0} ${color 9A9A9A}upl ${color FFFFFF}${upspeed wlan0} |

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen


TEXT

${color 9A9A9A}usr ${color FFFFFF}${execi 300 whoami}
${color 9A9A9A}upt ${color FFFFFF}$uptime_short
${color 9A9A9A}tmp ${color FFFFFF}${nvidia temp} degrees
${color 9A9A9A}adr ${color FFFFFF}${addr wlan0}
${color 9A9A9A}krn ${color FFFFFF}linux $kernel
${color 9A9A9A}ver ${color FFFFFF}ubuntu linux 9.10 $machine
$hr 
${color 9A9A9A}${cpugraph cpu1 10, 100}  ${cpugraph cpu2 10, 100}  cpu ${color FFFFFF}${cpu cpu1} ${color FFFFFF}| ${color 9A9A9A}cpu ${color FFFFFF}${cpu cpu2}
${color 9A9A9A}${downspeedgraph wlan0 10, 100}  ${upspeedgraph wlan0 10, 100}  upl ${color FFFFFF}${upspeed wlan0} ${color FFFFFF}| ${color 9A9A9A}dwn ${color FFFFFF}${downspeed wlan0}
${color 9A9A9A}${memgraph 10, 100}  ${fs_bar 10, 100 /}  ram ${color FFFFFF}${memperc}% ${color FFFFFF}| ${color 9A9A9A}hdd ${color FFFFFF}${fs_used_perc}%
```

Can't stop it from flickering though. Anybody have any tips?

### Post by gutterslob on 2009-12-22
> **The Real Dave said:**
> 

Can I be quite nosey and ask what that is in the background of the second shot? You starting up the matrix? :)

If using Ubuntu
**apt-get install cmatrix**
To run,
**cmatrix -C [color]**
*replace [color] red, green, blue, white, yellow or black.

I used to have terminator running cmatrix as my wallpaper on my desktop.... but it got old real fast...and it uses too much cpu to have it permanently running on my Atom netbook, anyway.

In other words, it's just eye-candy for the sake of screenshots. :P ...  better than the cow, at least.

> **myusername said:**
> gnome
The panel looks good with that wallpaper, but chromium probably needs a more better theme.
Still pretty nice.

---

### Post by sertse on 2009-12-25
Welcome back Kupo Finale, my favourite 3 gtk themes along with Macchiato and Elegant Brit/Blue. Also changed the wallpaper again.

[[img]http://omploader.org/tMzJ4cA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMzJ4cA)[[img]http://omploader.org/tMzJ4cQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMzJ4cQ)

I got my wallpaper from here [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1329193](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1329193) (I'm using the later version with lettering removed - the original thread with the idea came from [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1327790") ) I suggest you encourage him to submit it as part of the ubuntu artwork if you like it. I like to think it's the spiritual successor of the classic animal pictures in Hardy and Intrepid. There's also a version with a transparent background so you adapt it to your own tastes. 

Thing to look at in my busy shot. 1) Audacious gtk! - It's in 2.2, but I don't know if its arrived in Ubuntu yet? 2) I've decided that just because some apps aren't developed anymore is no reason to not use them - welcome back Mirage, best image viewer ever :P, and to think I persisted with gpicview for months just because of this....

Same question as this last time: Anyone else find their Internet going horribly slow while uploading on omploader? It goes fine as soon as it's finished...

### Post by hyperdude111 on 2009-12-25
> **gjoellee said:**
> Theme and Dock info plz :P

I have to admit that I'm cheating with the theme. The apps shown are gnome do and "gloobus-preview" Gloobus opens almost any popular filetype and has that custom theme as shown. My actual emerald theme is futurelooks 3.3 which is not shown in the screen. However I am trying to create my own emerald theme based of the gloobus UI but am a novice with emerald theming.

The dock is "docky" recently split from gnome do, it now has a separate PPA and more features. Here is the docky PPA [https://launchpad.net/~docky-core/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~docky-core/+archive/ppa) I am using it with the default theme in panel mode.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-12-25
> **koleoptero said:**
> They've always been there in the "customize theme" dialogue and the appearance settings too. At least since Gutsy.

I'm not referring to the lack of button icons: *usually*, regardless of whether you've got button icons turned on or off, dialog window buttons are always 'fat'.

### Post by yahrialb on 2009-12-25
This is my current desktop see attached thumbnails below

[IMG]http://imgur.com/JH3xf.jpg[/IMG]

[IMG]http://imgur.com/5WxhC.jpg[/IMG]

[IMG]http://imgur.com/Q671L.jpg[/IMG]

The Menu is GnoMenu [http://www.gtk-apps.org/content/show.php/GnoMenu+-+consolidated+menu+for+gnome?content=93056](http://www.gtk-apps.org/content/show.php/GnoMenu+-+consolidated+menu+for+gnome?content=93056)

The Menu selection is Lancelot built in

The Button selection is Dark Ubuntu [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Dark+ubuntu+button+for+GnoMenu?content=93141](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Dark+ubuntu+button+for+GnoMenu?content=93141)

The Icon selection is system icons instead of theme icons

The dock is AWN 0.40 [https://launchpad.net/~awn-testing/+archive/ppa]("https://launchpad.net/%7Eawn-testing/+archive/ppa")

Emerald is Kind Of Pink from the Kind Of Blue Suite it has been moded  for my taste in color [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Kind+of+Blue+Suite?content=46664](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Kind+of+Blue+Suite?content=46664)

The Gnome GTK is Crono Dark Pink [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Crono?content=105991](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Crono?content=105991)

The Icons are from the Ellanna Theme [http://www.bisigi-project.org/?p=209&#9001;=en]("http://www.bisigi-project.org/?p=209&lang=en")

The X11 Mouse Theme is Vienna 3 [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Vienna+3?content=83194](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Vienna+3?content=83194)

System Font is Zekton [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Zekton?content=50553](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Zekton?content=50553)

The wallpaper is from the Ellanna Theme [http://www.bisigi-project.org/?p=209&#9001;=en]("http://www.bisigi-project.org/?p=209&lang=en")

The folder thumbnails on the third screenshot is from cover thumbnailer  [http://software.flogisoft.com/cover-thumbnailer/en/](http://software.flogisoft.com/cover-thumbnailer/en/)

A few tips for cover thumbnailer is to put a image in the folder you want to display a cover and rename it folder or Folder

The image must end in .jpg not .jpeg to display the cover in nautilus

And if you run in to trouble with the images not displaying after awhile you can use bleachbit [http://bleachbit.sourceforge.net/](http://bleachbit.sourceforge.net/) to delete the thumbnails cache and then 
click reload in nautilus and the covers will regenerate

Note all of my screenshots are the maxium allowable size now 800x600 so the above images should not get deleted if they do refer to the attached images below

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/%3Ca%20href=http://www.freepicload.com/view.php?image=2bf6f8c7d38658c6338e821ce0d63f91.jpeg%20target=_blank%3E[IMG]http://www.freepicload.com/thumbs/2bf6f8c7d38658c6338e821ce0d63f91.jpeg[/IMG]

### Post by narf41 on 2009-12-27
> **armageddon08 said:**
> How did you get conky on KDE?

first you have to install feh
than use a script i found somewhere in the www:

```
#!/bin/bash
feh --bg-scale /home/narf/02Sys/3.jpg
conky -c /home/narf/02Sys/cnk_w/new/conky1
while inotifywait ~/.kde4/share/config/plasma-appletsrc; do
feh --bg-scale /home/narf/02Sys/3.jpg
done
```

make this script executable and put it to your autostart
in conky i use own_window_type override

---

> **DJ_Peng said:**

Thanks! The original is at 1680x1050, so you could do what I did and open it in GIMP, chop off the text at the bottom and set your background to "Fill Screen" so it squishes it. I'm at 1152x864.

I was bored this morning so I dug out some old wallpapers and fired up Compiz. This is running the Expo and Wallpaper plugins (unfortunately the Wallpaper plugin requires disabling Nautilus' drawing of the desktop, so you lose desktop icons and can only use the desktop as a folder via Places, but it sure looks cool!)...

### Post by hyperdude111 on 2009-12-27

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-12-27
> **hyperdude111 said:**
> @koleoptero 

Is your CPU monitor conky? If so could you please upload your .conkyrc, if it is something else please say and provide links because it looks great and I would love to try it on my desktop.

Thanks

No it's not conky. I got fed up with conky cause I installed it, put me previous config where it's supposed to go and it wouldn't even show the time, while mixing local with wireless network etc.

So I installed screenlets. Open a terminal and type: sudo apt-get install screenlets

Then it should appear in applications -> accessories. Open it and select the ring sensors. That's about it. Toy around with it to make it look as you like, it has several nice options.

---

### Post by hyperdude111 on 2009-12-27

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-12-28
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> did you arrange those apps yourself (almost looks like tiling), or is there a new feature in ob that has eluded me?

> **The Secret said:**
> Arranged manually, tough would love to see some kind of *manual tiling* ( tile when needed ) option in the future, too.

That would be a great feature, but while it is not implemented, add those keybinds to your rc.xml:
```
    <keybind key="C-W-Right">
      <action name="GrowToEdgeEast"/>
    </keybind>
    <keybind key="C-W-Left">
      <action name="GrowToEdgeWest"/>
    </keybind>
    <keybind key="C-W-Up">
      <action name="GrowToEdgeNorth"/>
    </keybind>
    <keybind key="C-W-Down">
      <action name="GrowToEdgeSouth"/>
    </keybind>
    <keybind key="C-W-space">
      <action name="GrowToEdgeEast"/>
      <action name="GrowToEdgeWest"/>
      <action name="GrowToEdgeNorth"/>
      <action name="GrowToEdgeSouth"/>
    </keybind>
```
The last one (Ctrl+Super+Space) is the best: it will "maximize" the focused window between the other windows in the current workspace.

### Post by Islington on 2009-12-28
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> is there a bespin icon set?

yes, its in the svn. cd into the icons folder and ./generate icons script. 

edit:

[quote="evilkastel"]
To get it, perform:

svn co [https://cloudcity.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/cloudcity](https://cloudcity.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/cloudcity)

in a konsole, and that will checkout the current rev of bespin. In there, there is an icons folder. TO get the icontheme do:

$cd icons
$./generate_kde_icons.sh

and copy the nmfnms folder to ~/yourusername/.kde4/share/icons

or the icon folder for your distro. Note that you can also compress the nmfnms folder and install it via the preferences dialog.
[/quote]

---

### Post by pelle.k on 2009-12-28
Using docky2 wity a custom theme. I must say i was more productive with the new AWN (development version). It's got more "applets". Especially a "gnome menu" and "notifications area".
So, i have to use a panel. It's 20 pixels high (with a custom background). I can't use a notification area, since it looks ridiculous at any height other than 24 pixels. I've used the alternative gnome menu, because that one can be used on panels smaller than 24 pixels. I tried storing some stuff in a "drawer" applet, but that thing doesn't play nice with compiz. It's rather ugly too, so i figured i could do without it anyway.
I hate the gnome panel, LOL.

### Post by 3Miro on 2009-12-30
This one thing that is very different from Windows/OSX, you are not using your computer for the same things as I am, your fingers/laptop keyboard is not the same as mine, your visual perception is not the same as mine. So why in the world would an interface that is good for me be good for you? The first thing that you will do when you get into a new car is to adjust the seat/steering wheel/mirrors, why do Apple and MS try to convince you that "their" look is the best for you.

The only good interface/look is the one that is 100% customizable, Linux isn't 100% there yet, but it is most of the way (and unlike the others it is at least trying).

The default look is the one with panels on the top and bottom. However, my laptop has a very short widescreen, so I prefer to put the top panel to the side. My wife on the other hand uses Mac at work, so she prefers more of a Mac look on her system (so she doesn't have to change very often). I have attached the three sreenshots.

There are many other possibilities.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-12-31
> **koleoptero said:**
> Goodbye 2009, a shitty year you were, I won't miss you at all.

What's the notification issue?

Also:
- By placing you panel 'centred' (while still keeping it, "full width"), you can get the notification area expander arrow/button to expand to the opposite side.
- Bolding your panel font, to match your window decorations, is as simple as adding:
```
style "xfce4-panel"
{
font_name=" bold" # note the whitespace preceding the word bold
}
widget_class "*Xfce*Panel*" style "xfce4-panel"
widget "*Xfce*Panel*" style "xfce4-panel"
class "*Xfce*Panel*" style "xfce4-panel"

``` to your ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2009-12-31
> **jorrieboy said:**
> wich theme do you use???
Light-Grey V2
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> What's the notification issue?

Also:
- By placing you panel 'centred' (while still keeping it, "full width"), you can get the notification area expander arrow/button to expand to the opposite side.
- Bolding your panel font, to match your window decorations, is as simple as adding:
```
style "xfce4-panel"
{
font_name=" bold" # note the whitespace preceding the word bold
}
widget_class "*Xfce*Panel*" style "xfce4-panel"
widget "*Xfce*Panel*" style "xfce4-panel"
class "*Xfce*Panel*" style "xfce4-panel"

``` to your ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file.
The notification area expands to whichever side every time I boot. It gives a sense of adventure I guess. :lolflag:
The notification issue is no longer an issue. I wanted to change the <x,y> coordinates it was set to appear to, cause the notifications were falling all over my double-wide panel. Now my panel is thin so it doesn't matter anymore. Also some programs don't show notifications anymore (like decibel) but again I don't really care.
I did that for the bold font, but it only bolded the desktop-switch applet and the active window button title. The inactive windows are still normal. Thanks though. Once again you save the day.
> **The Real Dave said:**
> Beautiful :) You make me really want to try XFCE :)
It's fun. You should try it, you can install it alongside whatever you use anyway.

P.S.: I just discovered that hibernation works in xubuntu as it is supposed to :KS (the damned power cable was pulled out from behind my laptop and suddenly as I was replying here the screen went black ](*,) cause I was out of battery)

> **koleoptero said:**
> I did that for the bold font, but it only bolded the desktop-switch applet and the active window button title. The inactive windows are still normal.
